### Post by gjoellee on 2009-05-31
Jaunty June...it is over so quickly!

> * Stay within the board rules, no matter how hot you may believe the wallpaper/screen shot to be.
* If you are going to quote, there isn't a need to quote an img-embeded picture - Just don't do it. Please just reference the post by page number/page link/etc.
* Off Topic Posts will be edited or removed.
* The desktops thread is not to be used as a means to post explicit or suggestive, and provocative images (they must be safe for your kids and/or boss to see). Please help to keep the thread relevant and safe to browse for everyone.
* The moderators of this forum reserve the right to edit or remove your posts as necessary so they may comply with our Community Rule set.
* Please use reduced-size thumbnails, where possible, out of respect for people running on lower bandwidth or screen resolutions.
* To avoid having users having to ask you for them. we request that you format your posts in the following order:

Themes: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).

Wallpaper: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).

Icons: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).

Programs: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).
Important Note: Any image posted that is over 800 x 600 will be removed! Use a thumbnail or use a text link to your image. If your image is removed, this is why.

Theme: Glow Water
Wallpaper: Got if from, [http://www.dualmonitorbackgrounds.com/](http://www.dualmonitorbackgrounds.com/)
Icons: Hydroxygen from [www.gnome-look.org](www.gnome-look.org)
Desktop: Arhc Linux, Xfce 4.6.1
Panel: xfce4-panel with panel cairo patch

Ubuntu Forums [Stylish](https://addons.mozilla.org/en-US/firefox/addon/2108) - opacity 9, background #333 (see code below)

```
@namespace url(http://www.w3.org/1999/xhtml);

@-moz-document domain("ubuntuforums.org"){

body{
background:#333 !important;
opacity:.9 !important;
}

}
```

### Post by K.Mandla on 2009-05-31
[[img]http://omploader.org/tMXIybg[/img]](http://omploader.org/vMXIybg)

Crux Linux on a 550Mhz Celeron with 192Mb and 120Gb 5400rpm drive. Video is 800x600 framebuffer only, no X. 

Running mplayer with the framebuffer video device, alsa, screen with the vertical split patch, alpine, rtorrent, iftop, elinks, calcurse, mc, centerim, mocp, htop, vim(wiki), hnb and some other stuff against kernel 2.6.29.3. Terminus font for the console.

Memory use floats around 32Mb. Boot time is under 13 seconds.

---

### Post by gashcr on 2009-05-31
> **K.Mandla said:**
> 


Memory use floats around 32Mb. Boot time is under 13 seconds.

amazing!!

here's mine :D It was a hard work, but I'm happy now

Wallpaper: WP Orange from deviantart
Icons: gnome-human
GTK: Kin (a little modified)
Metacity: Blendish (a little modified)
Fonts: Candice and Dejavu Sans Extralight
Screenlets: Ringsensors (with some camouflage :P ) & Circleclock
Rhythmbox desktop art
Gnome-Do
Compiz stars to blend with the wallpaper while giving some nice movement to the whole. Stars come from the left brilliant dots area, to finish the blending. 
No panels, no docks

### Post by iTrickU on 2009-06-01
My Desktop

[[img]http://img11.imageshack.us/img11/7909/31498693.png[/img]](http://img269.imageshack.us/img269/3679/54779692.png)

Theme:     QtCurve
Wallpaper: Included in KDE4
Icons:     Oxygen
Desktop:   KDE4/KDE3 with Thunar as the file manager

Tree Style Tab is a must have extension for anyone with a widescreen display, i found it very useful since i keep many tabs open when i'm browsing

Edit: QtCurve 0.63.0 (alpah/beta) was used in the screenshots, i got to test the new shading routine because i kept asking for it, the new shading routine is pretty tricky to work with in this version but it looks much better. If you want to try it you can get it from here: [http://rapidshare.com/files/239668245/qtcurve-0.63.0.tar.bz2](http://rapidshare.com/files/239668245/qtcurve-0.63.0.tar.bz2)

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2009-06-02
I find you can get by without alpha transparency just fine. Just set your opacity > 95%

---

### Post by Giant Speck on 2009-06-02
> **londonali1010 said:**
> Does anyone know how to get just one icon from another set into my current set? Because I changed to shiki-colours and I hate the battery icon (love everything else!) and I want to set it back to how it was when I was using Human.

Suggestions?

Take a look at the filename of the battery icon you want to implant into the theme.

Then navigate to /home/[yourusername]/.icons/[iconthemename]

Look through the folders to find an icon with the same filename and try to replace it with your preferred icon.  Then restart gnome-panel, or whatever panel you're using.

### Post by Mazza558 on 2009-06-02
> **Giant Speck said:**
> That isn't always the case, *especially* with Intel graphics cards.   I have an Intel 945GM and while Aero works flawlessly, Compiz Blur doesn't even work at all.  It freaks out, blacks out my windows and vertically inverts my display.

The proprietary NVIDIA drivers are some of the only drivers I know of that work well with the blur effect.

When designing FutureLooks, I wish I could design it with blurring in mind, but am forced to keep window decorations at 90% and above, in the interests of most people who want to use the theme.

I have looked through all the folders in /usr/share/icons/ and none of them have the battery icon that's currently being used, so I can't tell where it's coming from, and even more irritating, I can't seem to find the icon that it uses in the normal human theme.

I was thinking that if I can find the icon(s) it's using currently and the ones I want it to be, I would just replace it!  But it's not turning out to be that simple.  Unless I'm missing something...?

Am I the only one who hates the battery icon?!

---

### Post by perfectska04 on 2009-06-02
> **londonali1010 said:**
> Thanks, Giant Speck. But I haven't found what I need.  There are no folders in /home/username/.icons.  I have looked through all the folders in /usr/share/icons/ and none of them have the battery icon that's currently being used, so I can't tell where it's coming from, and even more irritating, I can't seem to find the icon that it uses in the normal human theme.

I was thinking that if I can find the icon(s) it's using currently and the ones I want it to be, I would just replace it!  But it's not turning out to be that simple.  Unless I'm missing something...?

Am I the only one who hates the battery icon?!

What icon set are you using? If it's gnome-colors, it doesn't have battery icons, as it inherits them from gnome-icon-theme. If you prefer the ones from Human, you can copy them from the /usr/share/icons/Human folder into the same folders of the set you're currently using.

### Post by cc8balla on 2009-06-03
> **GooglePlexity said:**
> So the time can be seen when there's a maximized window? The question is why have the time shown in Conky.  I guess the answer is because it looks nice, and can be larger.

I can relate to that. No worries, I was just asking :D 



> **Marlonsm said:**
> 
Just a question: where can I get this clock/date screenlet?
[[IMG]http://img37.imageshack.us/img37/5198/screenshoti.th.jpg[/IMG]](http://img37.imageshack.us/my.php?image=screenshoti.jpg)

That is my desktop, and that is conky displaying that. 

```
background yes
use_xft yes
xftfont ScalaSans-Caps:size=16
xftalpha 1
update_interval 1.0
total_run_times 0
own_window yes
own_window_transparent yes
own_window_class Conky
own_window_type override
own_window_hints undecorated,below,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager
double_buffer yes
minimum_size 280 200
maximum_width 320
draw_shades no
draw_outline no
draw_borders no
draw_graph_borders no
default_color 3e2b1c
default_shade_color black
default_outline_color white
alignment top_right
gap_x 22
gap_y 12
no_buffers yes
uppercase no
override_utf8_locale no
TEXT

${goto 20}${font ScalaSans-Caps:size=78conky}${time %I}${voffset -36}${font ScalaSans-Caps:bold:size=38}${time :%M}${voffset -18}${font ScalaSans-Caps:bold:size=18}${time %S}       

${goto 150}${voffset -10}${font ScalaSans-Caps:size=18}${time %A}      
${goto 150}${voffset 0}${time %B %d %Y}  


```

> **JECHO said:**

Thanks for the link.
I got Cover Art working,
In /.screenlets/NowPlaying/Players/Rythmbox.py 
change 
> return os.environ['HOME']+"/**.gnome2**/rhythmbox/covers/"+self.get_artist()+\
to
> return os.environ['HOME']+"/**.cache**/rhythmbox/covers/"+self.get_artist()+\

### Post by SomeGuyDude on 2009-06-04
> **londonali1010 said:**
> That looks pretty cool, actually, and I'd love to have my conky info up when I've got the windows maximised (which I almost always do because my screen is only 8.9"!!!  How did you do that?

I lucked out, actually. The panel I use on the upper-right there is tint2, which doesn't let windows maximize over it (obviously, since it's a panel). I tweaked the settings on both so the two of them would all fit in the same horizontal space. Since the windows can't cover tint, they can't cover conky.

If you're using GNOME and have the standard panel down below, I'm honestly not sure how it would be done. But if you're a flux/openbox user (or Compiz, like me), then it's pretty simple stuff.

---

### Post by GooglePlexity on 2009-06-04
> **SomeGuyDude said:**
> I lucked out, actually. The panel I use on the upper-right there is tint2, which doesn't let windows maximize over it (obviously, since it's a panel). I tweaked the settings on both so the two of them would all fit in the same horizontal space. Since the windows can't cover tint, they can't cover conky.

If you're using GNOME and have the standard panel down below, I'm honestly not sure how it would be done. But if you're a flux/openbox user (or Compiz, like me), then it's pretty simple stuff.

Gnome-panel actually has the necessary configuration options to make it not expand and be aligned to one side, so the same thing could be accomplished (except if you have a window list on your panel and it has too many entries it will overlap your conky).  The configuration options are in the appropriate panel in /apps/panel/toplevels.  I'll post a screenshot once I configure my conky.

---

### Post by Sarai the Geek on 2009-06-04
> **stanca said:**
> My first love,Ubuntu Ultimate Edition 1.8 look:
If you want, you can get rid of the drip shadow around your conky by adding this bit to the formatting section (before the TEXT marker):
```
own_window yes
own_window_transparent yes
own_window_type override
```

### Post by Marlonsm on 2009-06-04
> **cc8balla said:**
> 
That is my desktop, and that is conky displaying that. 

```
background yes
use_xft yes
xftfont ScalaSans-Caps:size=16
xftalpha 1
update_interval 1.0
total_run_times 0
own_window yes
own_window_transparent yes
own_window_class Conky
own_window_type override
own_window_hints undecorated,below,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager
double_buffer yes
minimum_size 280 200
maximum_width 320
draw_shades no
draw_outline no
draw_borders no
draw_graph_borders no
default_color 3e2b1c
default_shade_color black
default_outline_color white
alignment top_right
gap_x 22
gap_y 12
no_buffers yes
uppercase no
override_utf8_locale no
TEXT

${goto 20}${font ScalaSans-Caps:size=78conky}${time %I}${voffset -36}${font ScalaSans-Caps:bold:size=38}${time :%M}${voffset -18}${font ScalaSans-Caps:bold:size=18}${time %S}       

${goto 150}${voffset -10}${font ScalaSans-Caps:size=18}${time %A}      
${goto 150}${voffset 0}${time %B %d %Y}  


```

Thx a lot, it worked.

### Post by eightmillion on 2009-06-05
> **izizzle said:**
> Hey eightmillion which amarok theme is that? I really like the cover being displayed on the desktop and the amarok buttons.
That's just Amarok with the Bespin hacks applied. The cover art widget is a Superkaramba version of ThaFrame. I just wrote and uploaded a script that will build a Superkaramba theme file from the CAD skin. You can get it [here]("http://lyricsdownloader.googlecode.com/files/install.sh"). It requires having ThaFrame_by_OtisBee.zip in the same directory that it's run in. You can get that [here]("http://otisbee.deviantart.com/art/ThaFrame-116946137").

> **aschwerin.moses said:**
> Nice theme.. whats that widget to the bottom right corner?...
Thanks. That widget is the fifteen puzzle widget. You start with all of the pieces jumbled and then you have to slide them around to get them in the correct order. It's a fun distraction, but it's not very challenging.

---

### Post by eightmillion on 2009-06-05
> **Muppeteer said:**
> Yeah it wrote the file ok and it was executable...I think i read before you saying this app uses playwolf...And my playwolf is doing the same thing, no text or cover...I try to recompile it from source and it complains about nepomuk, kinda annoying cause this is an awesome skin.

It doesn't use playwolf, but they both use DBus, so you're probably having problems there. Try running this command:
```
python -c 'import dbus;print dbus.SessionBus().get_object("org.kde.amarok","/Player").GetMetadata()'
```

### Post by londonali1010 on 2009-06-06
> **heroidi said:**
> cool i like you'r conky config
Thanks :)
> **chucky chuckaluck said:**
> nice wallpaper and conky. have you considered a lighter gtk theme with that? maybe one of the auroras, or one of the less garish mac clones?
As a matter of fact, an earlier incarnation of this desktop had lovely milky white window decs with a modified Dust Sand gtk theme...Loved it, but got sick of it...I'll probably go back eventually!  But I'm diggin' the dark theme just at the moment :)
> **Islington said:**
> azel. also people still use awn? gnome-do docky is where it's at.
You know, people keep telling me that.  I'll probably have a go at gnome-do at some point, but I'm pretty happy with AWN for now!
> **Dawei87 said:**
> that conky looks great! would you mind sharing the conkyrc file?
Sure thing:
```
# Conky Configuration

background no
update_interval 1
total_run_times 0
own_window no
double_buffer yes
no_buffers yes
text_buffer_size 2048
cpu_avg_samples 2
net_avg_samples 2
override_utf8_locale yes
draw_shades no
draw_outline no
draw_borders no
draw_graph_borders yes
use_spacer none
minimum_size 0 0
alignment top_left
gap_x 12
gap_y 35
uppercase no
use_xft yes
xftfont DejaVu sans mono:size=8
xftalpha 0.8
default_color 3d3d3d
color1 b5b5b5

TEXT
${font}${color1}${execpi 1800 conkyForecast --location=XXXXXXX --template=/usr/share/conkyforecast/conkyForecast.template}${font}${color}
${voffset -85}${cpubar 15,214 cpu}
${voffset -19}${font}${color1} CPU ${cpu cpu}%
${voffset 3}${top pid 1} ${top name 1}${goto 188}${top cpu 1}
${top pid 2} ${top name 2}${goto 188}${top cpu 2}
${top pid 3} ${top name 3}${goto 188}${top cpu 3}${font}${color}
${membar 15,214}
${voffset -19}${font}${color1} MEM $memperc%
${voffset 3}${top_mem pid 1} ${top_mem name 1}${goto 188}${top_mem mem 1}
${top_mem pid 2} ${top_mem name 2}${goto 188}${top_mem mem 2}
${top_mem pid 3} ${top_mem name 3}${goto 188}${top_mem mem 3}${font}${color}

${voffset 400}${fs_bar 15,214 /}${goto 795}${downspeedgraph wlan0 15,214}
${voffset -19}${font}${color1} SSD ${fs_free /} free${goto 795} WLAN ${downspeed wlan0} kb/s${font}${color}
```
I also use the ConkyForecast script from here: [http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=869328](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=869328), with the following template:
```
${goto 760}${font MoonPhases:size=18}[--datatype=WF] ${font ConkyWeather:size=24}[--datatype=WF --startday=1 --endday=4 --spaces=3]${font}
${voffset -2}${goto 760}${offset -9}[--datatype=DW --startday=0 --endday=4 --shortweekday --centeredwidth=8]
${goto 760}${offset -2}Night${offset 14}[--datatype=HT --startday=1 --hideunits --centeredwidth=3]/[--datatype=LT --startday=1 --hideunits --centeredwidth=3]${offset 14}[datatype=HT --startday=2 --hideunits --centeredwidth=3]/[--datatype=LT --startday=2 --hideunits --centeredwidth=3]${offset 14}[--datatype=HT --startday=3 --hideunits --centeredwidth=3]/[--datatype=LT --startday=3 --hideunits --centeredwidth=3]${offset 14}[--datatype=HT --startday=4 --hideunits --centeredwidth=3]/[--datatype=LT --startday=4 --hideunits --centeredwidth=3]

```
I should say, it's all custom to fit my screen (1024x600 netbook), so it will take a good deal of tweaking if you want it to look right!

---

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2009-06-06
> **aschwerin.moses said:**
> Buddy, i did try to use the conky scrips from ur site but could not get the RSS conky. I really like the RSS conky that u have at the bottom, please paste the script if u dont mind... thank you.
I think your mistake was expecting the code to appear in the preview. You needed to download the actual file to your computer and open it up with a text editor.

```
own_window_title conkyrss

max_user_text 20000

use_xft yes
xftfont Sans:size=6
override_utf8_locale yes
xftalpha 1

update_interval 1
draw_shades no
default_shade_color 2525ff
draw_outline no
default_outline_color 2525ff
draw_borders no
stippled_borders no
border_margin 0
border_width 1

no_buffers yes
uppercase no
double_buffer yes
use_spacer none

default_color ffffff
color0 ffffff
color1 cfdfdf
color2 bfbfbf
color3 0a0a0a
color4 080808

own_window yes
own_window_colour 080808
own_window_transparent no
own_window_type dock
own_window_hints undecorate,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager,below
background yes
alignment bottom_left
gap_x 1
gap_y 20
minimum_size 1440 0

TEXT
${voffset -3}
${voffset -3}${font Sans:bold:size=7}${color}${goto 20}News Feed 1${goto 120}${color ff7e00}${voffset 0}${fs_bar 6,15 /fakelol/}${color}${goto 121}${voffset -1}rss${voffset 1}${goto 220}News Feed 2${goto 320}${color ff7e00}${voffset 0}${fs_bar 6,15 /fakelol/}${color}${goto 321}${voffset -1}rss${voffset 1}${goto 420}News Feed 3${goto 520}${color ff7e00}${voffset 0}${fs_bar 6,15 /fakelol/}${color}${goto 521}${voffset -1}rss${voffset 1}${goto 620}News Feed 4${goto 720}${color ff7e00}${voffset 0}${fs_bar 6,15 /fakelol/}${color}${goto 721}${voffset -1}rss${voffset 1}${goto 820}News Feed 5${goto 920}${color ff7e00}${voffset 0}${fs_bar 6,15 /fakelol/}${color}${goto 921}${voffset -1}rss${voffset 1}${goto 1020}News Feed 6${goto 1120}${color ff7e00}${voffset 0}${fs_bar 6,15 /fakelol/}${color}${goto 1121}${voffset -1}rss${voffset 1}${goto 1220}News Feed 7${goto 1320}${color ff7e00}${voffset 0}${fs_bar 6,15 /fakelol/}${color}${goto 1321}${voffset -1}rss${voffset 1}${font}${color1}

### Post by m00se3724 on 2009-06-06
> **heroidi said:**
> What concy config are you using here can you pm it to me or post it

```
# System stats bar

# Create own window instead of using desktop (required in nautilus)
own_window yes
own_window_type override
own_window_transparent yes
own_window_hints undecorated,below,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager
 
# Use double buffering (reduces flicker, may not work for everyone)
double_buffer yes
 
# fiddle with window
use_spacer right

# Use Xft?
use_xft yes
xftfont unDotum:size=8
xftalpha 0.8
text_buffer_size 2048
 
# Update interval in seconds
update_interval 3.0
 
# Minimum size of text area
minimum_size 250 5
maximum_width 255
 
# Draw shades?
draw_shades no
 
# Text stuff
draw_outline no # amplifies text if yes
draw_borders no
uppercase no # set to yes if you want all text to be in uppercase
 
# Stippled borders?
stippled_borders 3
 
# border margins
border_margin 9
 
# border width
border_width 10
 
# Default colors 
default_color grey
  
# Text alignment, other possible values are commented
alignment top_left
 
# Gap between borders of screen
gap_x 1020
gap_y 60


# Possible variables to be used:
#
#      Variable         Arguments                  Description                
#  acpiacadapter                     ACPI ac adapter state.                   
#  acpifan                           ACPI fan state                           
#  acpitemp                          ACPI temperature.                        
#  adt746xcpu                        CPU temperature from therm_adt746x       
#  adt746xfan                        Fan speed from therm_adt746x             
#  battery           (num)           Remaining capasity in ACPI or APM        
#                                    battery. ACPI battery number can be      
#                                    given as argument (default is BAT0).     
#  buffers                           Amount of memory buffered                
#  cached                            Amount of memory cached                  
#  color             (color)         Change drawing color to color            
#  cpu                               CPU usage in percents                    
#  cpubar            (height)        Bar that shows CPU usage, height is      
#                                    bar's height in pixels                   
#  downspeed         net             Download speed in kilobytes              
#  downspeedf        net             Download speed in kilobytes with one     
#                                    decimal                                  
#  exec              shell command   Executes a shell command and displays    
#                                    the output in torsmo. warning: this      
#                                    takes a lot more resources than other    
#                                    variables. I'd recommend coding wanted   
#                                    behaviour in C and posting a patch :-).  
#  execi             interval, shell Same as exec but with specific interval. 
#                    command         Interval can't be less than              
#                                    update_interval in configuration.        
#  fs_bar            (height), (fs)  Bar that shows how much space is used on 
#                                    a file system. height is the height in   
#                                    pixels. fs is any file on that file      
#                                    system.                                  
#  fs_free           (fs)            Free space on a file system available    
#                                    for users.                               
#  fs_free_perc      (fs)            Free percentage of space on a file       
#                                    system available for users.              
#  fs_size           (fs)            File system size                         
#  fs_used           (fs)            File system used space                   
#  hr                (height)        Horizontal line, height is the height in 
#                                    pixels                                   
#  i2c               (dev), type, n  I2C sensor from sysfs (Linux 2.6). dev   
#                                    may be omitted if you have only one I2C  
#                                    device. type is either in (or vol)       
#                                    meaning voltage, fan meaning fan or temp 
#                                    meaning temperature. n is number of the  
#                                    sensor. See /sys/bus/i2c/devices/ on     
#                                    your local computer.                     
#  kernel                            Kernel version                           
#  loadavg           (1), (2), (3)   System load average, 1 is for past 1     
#                                    minute, 2 for past 5 minutes and 3 for   
#                                    past 15 minutes.                         
#  machine                           Machine, i686 for example                
#  mails                             Mail count in mail spool. You can use    
#                                    program like fetchmail to get mails from 
#                                    some server using your favourite         
#                                    protocol. See also new_mails.            
#  mem                               Amount of memory in use                  
#  membar            (height)        Bar that shows amount of memory in use   
#  memmax                            Total amount of memory                   
#  memperc                           Percentage of memory in use              
#  new_mails                         Unread mail count in mail spool.         
#  nodename                          Hostname                                 
#  outlinecolor      (color)         Change outline color                     
#  pre_exec          shell command   Executes a shell command one time before 
#                                    torsmo displays anything and puts output 
#                                    as text.                                 
#  processes                         Total processes (sleeping and running)   
#  running_processes                 Running processes (not sleeping),        
#                                    requires Linux 2.6                       
#  shadecolor        (color)         Change shading color                     
#  stippled_hr       (space),        Stippled (dashed) horizontal line        
#                    (height)        
#  swapbar           (height)        Bar that shows amount of swap in use     
#  swap                              Amount of swap in use                    
#  swapmax                           Total amount of swap                     
#  swapperc                          Percentage of swap in use                
#  sysname                           System name, Linux for example           
#  time              (format)        Local time, see man strftime to get more 
#                                    information about format                 
#  totaldown         net             Total download, overflows at 4 GB on     
#                                    Linux with 32-bit arch and there doesn't 
#                                    seem to be a way to know how many times  
#                                    it has already done that before torsmo   
#                                    has started.                             
#  totalup           net             Total upload, this one too, may overflow 
#  updates                           Number of updates (for debugging)        
#  upspeed           net             Upload speed in kilobytes                
#  upspeedf          net             Upload speed in kilobytes with one       
#                                    decimal                                  
#  uptime                            Uptime                                   
#  uptime_short                      Uptime in a shorter format               
#
#  seti_prog                         Seti@home current progress
#  seti_progbar      (height)        Seti@home current progress bar
#  seti_credit                       Seti@hoome total user credit
#
#
# variable is given either in format $variable or in ${variable}. Latter
# allows characters right after the variable and must be used in network
# stuff because of an argument
#
 
# stuff after 'TEXT' will be formatted on screen
 
TEXT
$color
${color #689098}${font A bite:size=24}SYSTEM
${voffset -45}${hr 2}$font$color
$sysname $kernel $alignr $machine
Intel Core Duo $alignr${freq_g cpu0}Ghz
Uptime $alignr${uptime_short}
File System $alignr${fs_type}

${voffset -5}${color #79cbd6}${font A bite:size=24}PROCESSOR
${voffset -45}${hr 2}$font $color
CPU1  ${cpu cpu1}% ${color #a6a6a6}${cpubar cpu1}$color

TOP PROCESSES
${top_mem name 1}${alignr}${top mem 1} %
${top_mem name 2}${alignr}${top mem 2} %
${top_mem name 3}${alignr}${top mem 3} %
${top_mem name 4}${alignr}${top mem 4} %
 
${voffset -5}${color #cae186} ${font A bite:size=24}MEM DISK
${voffset -45}${hr 2}$font $color
RAM: $alignc $mem / $memmax $alignr $memperc%
${color #a6a6a6}$membar$color
SWAP: $alignc $swap / $swapmax $alignr $swapperc%
${color #a6a6a6}$swapbar$color
/ $alignc ${fs_used /} / ${fs_size /} $alignr ${fs_used_perc /}%
${color #a6a6a6}${fs_bar /}$color
Home $alignc ${fs_used /home} / ${fs_size /home} $alignr ${fs_used_perc /home}%
${color #a6a6a6}${fs_bar /home}$color

${voffset -5}${color #fbd109}${font A bite:size=24}NETWORK
${voffset -45}${hr 2}$font $color
External IP $alignr ${execi 300 wget www.whatismyip.com/automation/n09230945.asp -O - -q}
IP on eth0 $alignr ${addr eth0}
IP on wlan0 $alignr ${addr wlan0}
Download Speed $alignr ${downspeed eth0} kb/s
Uploaded Speed $alignr ${upspeed eth0} kb/s
Total Downloads $alignr  ${totaldown eth0}
Total Uploads $alignr  ${totalup eth0}

${color #fe94a8} ${font A bite:size=24}WEATHER
${voffset -45}${hr 2}$font $color
$alignr ${execi 300 conkyForecast --location="CODE HERE" --datatype=CN}, ${execi 300 conkyForecast --location="CODE HERE" --datatype=CO} 
$alignr Last Update: ${execi 300 conkyForecast --location="CODE HERE" --hideunits --datatype=LU -m 0 --imperial}
${voffset -40}${color #a6a6a6}${font ConkyWeather:size=85}${execi 300 conkyForecast --location="CODE HERE" --imperial --datatype=WF}$color
$font${voffset -167}${alignr}Wind: ${execi 300 conkyForecast --imperial --location="CODE HERE" --datatype=WS} ${execi 300 conkyForecast --datatype=WD}
${alignr}Humidity: ${execi 300 conkyForecast --location="CODE HERE" --imperial --datatype=HM}
${alignr}Precipitation: ${execi 300 conkyForecast --imperial --location="CODE HERE" --startday=0 --datatype=PC}
${alignr}Sunrise: ${execi 300 conkyForecast --location="CODE HERE" --datatype=SR}
${alignr}Sunset: ${execi 300 conkyForecast --location="CODE HERE" --datatype=SS}
${alignc 30}${execi 300 conkyForecast --location="CODE HERE" --datatype=CT}: ${execi 300 conkyForecast --location="CODE HERE" --imperial --hideunits --datatype=HT} $font $alignr Feels Like: ${execi 300 conkyForecast --location="CODE HERE" --imperial --datatype=LT}

${alignc 7}${execi 300 conkyForecast --imperial --location="CODE HERE" --startday=0 --endday=4 --spaces=12 --datatype=DW -w}
${color #a6a6a6}${font ConkyWeather:size=26}${execi 300 conkyForecast --location="CODE HERE" --spaces=2 --startday=0 --endday=4 --centeredwidth=1 --datatype=WF}$font$color
${alignc 110}${execi 300 conkyForecast --imperial --location="CODE HERE" --startday=0 --hideunits --datatype=HT}/${execi 300 conkyForecast --imperial --location="CODE HERE" --startday=0 --hideunits --datatype=LT}${alignc 0}${execi 300 conkyForecast --imperial --location="CODE HERE" --startday=1 --hideunits --datatype=HT}/${execi 300 conkyForecast --startday=1 --hideunits --location="CODE HERE" --imperial --datatype=LT}${alignc -40}${execi 300 conkyForecast --startday=2 --hideunits --imperial --location="CODE HERE" --datatype=HT}/${execi 300 conkyForecast --imperial --location="CODE HERE" --startday=2 --hideunits --datatype=LT}${alignc -75}${execi 300 conkyForecast --imperial --hideunits --location="CODE HERE" --startday=3 --datatype=HT}/${execi 300 conkyForecast --imperial --location="CODE HERE" --startday=3 --hideunits --datatype=LT}${alignc -105}${execi 300 conkyForecast --imperial --location="CODE HERE" --startday=4 --hideunits --datatype=HT}/${execi 300 conkyForecast --imperial --location="CODE HERE" --startday=4 --hideunits --datatype=LT}

### Post by spiceminesofkessel on 2009-06-06
Theme: [OverGlossed]("http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Overglossed?content=74813")
Icons: [Black-Wite 2 Style]("http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/black-white+2+Style?content=72619")
Wallpaper: I made it myself using [GIMP]("http://gimp.org"). It's on my [website]("http://spiceminesofkessel.com/spices") (Graphics section).
Programs: Most are obvious, but Steam is installed using [CrossOver Games]("http://codeweavers.com").

> **Viva said:**
> Details please..
 
GTK: Azel from gnome look. in gtkrc commented out ```
include "no-globalmenurc"
```and all 3 panel options.

Emerald: attached.
Icons: Mac4lin
Panel: globalmenu applet, background attached
gnome: turned off interface icons to text only; set ```
/desktop/gnome/interface/buttons_have_icons
``` to false in gconf-editor
wallpaper: [http://www.flickr.com/photos/bogenfreund/1060076354/sizes/o/](http://www.flickr.com/photos/bogenfreund/1060076354/sizes/o/)

### Post by sertse on 2009-06-06
It's emesene

There is an official version in the repo, but it's no longer developed as the author is doing a rewrite which isn't released yet. There is also a unofficial "community version" in the meantime from [http://forum.emesene.org/](http://forum.emesene.org/) with [https://launchpad.net/~bjfs/+archive/ppa](https://launchpad.net/~bjfs/+archive/ppa) as a ppa.

---

### Post by Tipped OuT on 2009-06-06
> **dullo said:**
> what is that msn icon? how can you install windows live messenger on ubuntu, or is that something different? if so what are you using?

It's called Emesene. It's the best MSN Messenger replacement in my opinion. To install it, go to Applications< Add/Remove and type in the search box "Emesene". Check the little box next to it and click "apply".

---

### Post by neo_1in on 2009-06-06
> **yabbadabbadont said:**
> Please share the tint2rc config.
Here...
```
#---------------------------------------------
# TINT2 CONFIG FILE
#---------------------------------------------

#---------------------------------------------
# BACKGROUND AND BORDER
#---------------------------------------------
rounded = 2
border_width = 2
background_color = #feddef 40
border_color = #654456 40

rounded = 2
border_width = 1
background_color = #ffffff 0
border_color = #000000 0

rounded = 2
border_width = 1
background_color = #123321 25
border_color = #aaaaff 30

#---------------------------------------------
# PANEL
#---------------------------------------------
panel_monitor = all
panel_position = bottom center
panel_size = 92% 42
panel_margin = 1 1
panel_padding = 4 2
font_shadow = 0
panel_background_id = 1

#---------------------------------------------
# TASKBAR
#---------------------------------------------
taskbar_mode = single_monitor
taskbar_padding = 0 0 2
taskbar_background_id = 0

#---------------------------------------------
# TASKS
#---------------------------------------------
task_icon = 1
task_text = 0
task_width = 43
task_centered = 1
task_padding = 6 3
task_font = (null)
task_font_color = #000000 75
task_active_font_color = #ffffff 75
task_background_id = 2
task_active_background_id = 3

#---------------------------------------------
# SYSTRAYBAR
#---------------------------------------------
systray_padding = 0 4 5
systray_background_id = 0

#---------------------------------------------
# CLOCK
#---------------------------------------------
time1_format = %a %I:%M %p
time1_font = Liberation Sans Bold 12
#time2_format = %A %d %B
time2_font = (null)
clock_font_color = #feddef 100
clock_padding = 6 2
clock_background_id = 3

#---------------------------------------------
# BATTERY
#---------------------------------------------
battery = 0
battery_low_status = 0
battery_low_cmd = (null)
bat1_font = (null)
bat2_font = (null)
battery_font_color = #000000 0
battery_padding = 2 2
battery_background_id = 0

#---------------------------------------------
# MOUSE ACTION ON TASK
#---------------------------------------------
mouse_middle = none
mouse_right = none
mouse_scroll_up = toggle
mouse_scroll_down = iconify

```

---

### Post by londonali1010 on 2009-06-07
See? It took me all of about two days to get sick of the dark theme, and now I'm back on ethereal white.

Actually, it was interesting, I found a thread about improving graphics performance on Intel graphics cards in Jaunty ([http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=1130582]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=1130582")), so I had a go with the hope that it would allow me to get blur to work, but to no avail :(  My poor little netbook ain't got enough juice!  But it might work for some others with Intel graphics who want to get blur to work...There are posts on the thread that imply it has worked for them.

Anyway, Here's my current setup:
[ATTACH]116701[/ATTACH][ATTACH]116702[/ATTACH]
GTK Theme: Dust Sand (panel colour/transparency adjusted to match window decs)
Window Decorator: Custom Emerald, based on White Mod
Icons: Shiki-Wise, inherits Human
Wallpaper: erm, don't remember...I *think* I got it off Zixpk ([http://www.zixpk.com/2008/04/picture-of-meaning.html](http://www.zixpk.com/2008/04/picture-of-meaning.html))

Dock: Cairo-Dock with custom theme, modified from something but so extensively it may as well have been the default theme I modified from :P

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2009-06-08
> **geekygirl said:**
> Not much has changed, just added Ubuntu System Panel :)

[IMG]http://farm4.static.flickr.com/3351/3607565284_b064d03a30.jpg[/IMG]
[Click Here For Full Size]("http://farm4.static.flickr.com/3351/3607565284_65499030ed_o.png")

[IMG]http://farm4.static.flickr.com/3411/3606744527_a8f4de190d.jpg[/IMG]
[Click Here For Full Size]("http://farm4.static.flickr.com/3411/3606744527_c7fb858993_o.png")

That thing strikes me as a usability nightmare: 
- wildly inconsistent layout (some icons are huge, some are small, some are just plain missing eg. app categories)
- categories are poorly defined from one another (GtkFrames exist for a reason)
- too much information is on-screen (kernel, screen res, time info is just wank)
- and the order of categories just serves to slow down performing simple tasks (why are User, Sys management and Settings options closest to the menu button and apps/places furthest away? Who spends the majority of their time at the computer configuring their system {possibly not the best thread to be asking this question in >.>}?).

Fundamentally good idea and I wouldn't mind something like that for Xfce but the execution leaves a lot to be desired.

---

### Post by Sarai the Geek on 2009-06-08
> **izizzle said:**
> Is there any way to install Docky in Kubuntu without having to install gnome-desktop?
Hmm, libgnomedesktop2.20cil is listed as a dependency for gnome-do and thus you probably won't be able to work around it. But remember that gnome-desktop is not the same as ubuntu-desktop, that is it doesn't contain a bunch of programs that you as a KDE user probably won't end up using.

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2009-06-09
> **Tipped OuT said:**
> Wow, that's pretty cool! Is Fluxbox hard to use? I might try it.

Easy to use; PITA to configure. Granted. I think at least part of that has to do with some weird bug with my system. I get weird X issues when trying to run Openbox or Fluxbox. If you find Fluxbox daunting, you can get a pretty similar experience running Xfce, without all the manual config file editing.

On Windows I run [bbClean](http://wiki.bb4win.org/wiki/BBClean), which is a clone of Blackbox, which Fluxbox in based upon. On Windows it's more of a complete shell, with a variety of plugins that extend both the window management capabilities and allows you to have a lot of 'panels' and 'widgets'. bbClean and the other BB4WIN derivatives, while buggy, are the only way I can use Windows these days without wanting to punch the screen.

> **edthefox said:**
> Ubuntu 9.04

[IMG]http://lh5.ggpht.com/_d3B9dvVdQ94/Si09G7SctxI/AAAAAAAAAUs/njP3mzM0Jl0/s800/desktop1.jpeg[/IMG]

Nice. Could I possibly get a link on that wall?

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2009-06-09
> **pwnst*r said:**
> how is bbclean different from bbLean?  i use bblean on windows on a lappie at home

Mostly it just incorporates a couple of former plugins (menu icons, a bbleanskin mod), plus it has a few bug fixes. It's a little smoother. There's also a couple of mods of bbClean (yes, a mod of a mod of a mod) that add things like split gradients and pixmap theming but these apparently break quite a few plugins.

---

### Post by sertse on 2009-06-09
> **Tipped OuT said:**
> Wow, that's pretty cool! Is Fluxbox hard to use? I might try it.

Not hard to use, initial setup might take a bit of effort. Config files are clearest I know though; it is pretty easy to learn what to do just by looking at them and editing it to your needs. For me, the main effort was making my menu; it'll autocreate one in Ubuntu but imo it isn't categorised too well, so there'll be a bit of rearranging there to get it to suit you.

### Post by captainmnb on 2009-06-09
Theme: Shiki colors (human)
Wallpaper: [http://barmin.deviantart.com/art/Darwin-wallpaper-112143848](http://barmin.deviantart.com/art/Darwin-wallpaper-112143848)
Icons: Meliae white
Dock: gnome-panel with DockbarX ([http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/DockbarX?content=101604](http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/DockbarX?content=101604) -- it's the best non-composited dock I've been able to find)
Custom conky (with a few positioning bugs to work out)
And in the top right is the absolutely essential Thunderbird New Mail Icon extension.
No compositing.  It just slows things down and causes conflicts with other programs, especially since I have an ATI card.

### Post by eightmillion on 2009-06-09
> **izizzle said:**
> Weird....Even when I use superkaramba to manage my karambas, it still does not stay where I want it to. There is like a margin on the left edge of my screen. If I reload the theme it keeps a margin between itself and the desktop's edge. Any ideas?

The reason it does that is because the shadow extends a bit farther than it appears. When you move it really close to the edge of the screen, then part of the widget is off screen. When you reload it or restart Superkaramba, it moves it back to where the whole thing is being drawn on screen. Is there some reason you have to reload it? Because it should just stay in its place after you moved it.

### Post by Daisuke_Aramaki on 2009-06-09
@TippedOut

thanks for the comment. Fluxbox is pretty easy to setup. and yes, it will take a little while to get used to the configuration, but once you know your way around, its pretty easy. 

everything is done with simple text files. i have a minimal fluxbox setup, and i am so much used to the keyboard, that i am so not interested in setting up the menu for each program that i have installed. just one simple key binding for gmrun takes care of all my app launching needs. 

@Armageddon

the fluxbox theme is Fawn made by thrynk. i modified it to suit my urxvt colors. 

gtk is azra murrine brown like. its available over at gnome-look. keep in mind, its beta as the author had said, and its pretty buggy, especially the drop down menu. so one might have to work on the gtkrc.

---

### Post by Sarai the Geek on 2009-06-10
> **Delirium_Trigger said:**
> Still working on it, but it's coming along nicely.
Please crit :D

I rather like the wallpaper actually, but I'm kind of a sucker for transparent layouts with grass backgrounds. 
The only thing I don't much care for on this screenie is the overabundance of icons in the top panel. You should try a transparent or semi-transparent dock on the bottom to corral those shortcuts rather than cramming them next to the menu.
Try avant-window-navigator, that's the best I've used that provides good-looking transparency.

> **etnlIcarus said:**
> How'd you get the clock text to display in two different colours?

There's a gconf key: on my computer it's /apps/panel/applets/clock_screen0/prefs/custom_format and I changed it to:

```

<span color="#6482AB" size="smaller">%a %e %b</span> %l:%M %p

```

You also need to change "format" to "custom".

---

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2009-06-10
Just and FYI: if anyone is struggling with that VLC-not-embedding bug:

deb [http://ppa.launchpad.net/medigeek/ppa/ubuntu](http://ppa.launchpad.net/medigeek/ppa/ubuntu) jaunty main

Apparently causes an occasional crash but I've had the PPA build of VLC installed for about a week and it hasn't crashed once yet.

### Post by Giant Speck on 2009-06-11
I didn't change anything about the theme itself from the last screenshot, but I did change the following:

CAIRO-DOCK:  I made some new icons.  The GIMP and Synaptic ones look a bit funny, though.

EMERALD:  I brought back the rounded top-left corner that was there before I released Macchiato 0.3.

FIREFOX:  I extracted the tab-specific portions of a userstyle I found called "Chrome Skin" to make it match my theme.

FONT:  I changed the font to Calibri, size 8.

I'm also thinking about making a conky based off of my cairo-dock icons.

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2009-06-11
The dark tabbar adds some needed contrast; makes the theme more striking. IMO, it would be a good idea to replicate that effect with the panel. Granted, if you're going to add contrast with a darker bit, achieving that same contrast with froth becomes redundant and potentially counter-productive to the theme's overall elegance (I can't think of many three-tone themes that work well, except perhaps shiki colours).

---

Okay, I've moved the files to Google Code so there shouldn't be any more warnings. I've also adapted a metacity theme to mimic the emerald version, so if you download the latest from GNOME-look you should be treated to a better metacity.

However, the metacity theme still has a few bugs, given that I've only spent about 30 minutes adapting it:

- There is little distinguishing active and inactive windows if you do not have compiz enabled (the gradient colors don't change between active/inactive windows)
- Maximized windows are still curved at the edges.

### Post by zyxyellowxyz on 2009-06-12
[[IMG]http://i20.photobucket.com/albums/b216/zyxyellowxyz/0000000/th_Screenshot.png[/IMG]]("http://i20.photobucket.com/albums/b216/zyxyellowxyz/0000000/Screenshot.png")
(click for full view)

GTK: modified Murrine7 [http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Murrine7?content=105521]("http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Murrine7?content=105521")
Wallpaper: Tux vs Windows 7 Fish [http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Tux+vs+Windows+7+Fish?content=104629]("http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Tux+vs+Windows+7+Fish?content=104629")
Icons: modified Sewen Icon Theme [http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Sewen+Icon+Theme?content=99285]("http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Sewen+Icon+Theme?content=99285")
Cursor: Aero Drop Shadow [http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Aero+Mouse+Cursors+with+Drop+Shadow?content=67833]("http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Aero+Mouse+Cursors+with+Drop+Shadow?content=67833")
Cairo-Dock Theme: Clear (came with Cairo-Dock when I installed the themes package; modified with different applets and launchers)
Emerald: Who Need Windows 7 ? [http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Who+Needs+Windows+7+%3F?content=105399]("http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Who+Needs+Windows+7+%3F?content=105399")
Conkyrc: (took out my location data, well, because I wanted to)```
# SuzyQ's Conky configuration

background yes
use_xft yes
xftfont Sans:size=8
xftalpha 0.8
update_interval 5.0
total_run_times 0
own_window yes
own_window_type override
own_window_transparent yes
#own_window_colour black
own_window_hints undecorated,below,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager
double_buffer yes
minimum_size 200 
draw_shades no
draw_outline no
draw_borders no
draw_graph_borders no
border_margin 2
border_width 1
default_color white
default_shade_color black
default_outline_color black
#alignment middle_right
alignment top_right
#alignment middle_left
gap_x 12
gap_y 0
no_buffers yes
uppercase no
cpu_avg_samples 2
net_avg_samples 2
override_utf8_locale yes
use_spacer none
show_graph_scale no
show_graph_range yes
text_buffer_size 1024
color0 B9D1EA
color2 FFFFFF
color1 1330c8
color3 191547
color4 D2691E
color5 CCCCCC
color6 FFCC00
color7 333333
color8 000000
color9 FFA500

# stuff after 'TEXT' will be formatted on screen

TEXT
${font Domestic Manners:style=Bold:size=30}${color1}SuzyQ's PC
${voffset -50}$stippled_hr
${voffset -45}${color5}${font Sans:style=Bold:size=10}DATE/TIME${color3}${hr 3}${color2}
${font Radio Space:size=15}${alignc}${time %A %B %d %Y}
${alignc}${time %I:%M %P}
${color5}${font Sans:style=Bold:size=10}WEATHER${color3}${hr 3}${color2}
${font}${alignc}${execpi 30 conkyForecast --location=XXXXXXXX --datatype=CN}, ${execpi 30 conkyForecast --location=XXXXXXXX --datatype=CO}
${voffset 0}${font ConkyWeather:size=20}${execpi 30 conkyForecast --location=XXXXXXXX --datatype=WF}${voffset -10}${offset 0}${font}${alignr}${execpi 30 conkyForecast --location=XXXXXXXX --datatype=CT}
${voffset 10}${font MoonPhases:size=12}${execpi 30 conkyForecast --location=XXXXXXXX --datatype=MF}${voffset -5}${offset 0}${font}${alignr}${execpi 30 conkyForecast --location=XXXXXXXX --datatype=MP}
${font}Temperature:${alignr}${execpi 30 conkyForecast --location=XXXXXXXX --datatype=HT --imperial} (Feels Like ${execpi 30 conkyForecast --location=XXXXXXXX --datatype=LT --imperial})
Humidity:${alignr}${execpi 30 conkyForecast --location=XXXXXXXX --datatype=HM}
Precipirarion Chance:${alignr}${execpi 30 conkyForecast --location=XXXXXXXX --datatype=PC}
Dew Point:${alignr}${execpi 30 conkyForecast --location=XXXXXXXX --datatype=DP --imperial}
Visibility:${alignr}${execpi 30 conkyForecast --location=XXXXXXXX --datatype=VI --imperial}
Wind:${alignr}${execpi 30 conkyForecast --location=XXXXXXXX --datatype=WD --imperial} (${execpi 30 conkyForecast --location=XXXXXXXX --datatype=WS --imperial})
UV-Index:${alignr}${execpi 30 conkyForecast --location=XXXXXXXX --datatype=UI} (${execpi 30 conkyForecast --location=XXXXXXXX --datatype=UT})
Barometer:${alignr}${execpi 30 conkyForecast --location=XXXXXXXX --datatype=BR --imperial} (${execpi 30 conkyForecast --location=XXXXXXXX --datatype=BD})
Daylight:${alignr}${execpi 30 conkyForecast --location=XXXXXXXX --datatype=SR}-${execpi 30 conkyForecast --location=XXXXXXXX --datatype=SS}
${font Sans:style=Bold:size=10}${color5}SYSTEM${color3}${hr 3}${color2}
${voffset 0}${font}Hostname:${alignr}${nodename}
Kernel:${alignr}${kernel}
Uptime:${alignr}${uptime}
${color2}CPU1:${alignr}${cpu cpu1}%
${color3}${cpubar cpu1}
${color2}CPU2:${alignr}${cpu cpu2}%
${color3}${cpubar cpu2}
${color2}RAM:${alignc}${mem}/${memmax}${alignr}${memperc}%
${color3}${membar}
${color5}${font Sans:style=Bold:size=10}FILE SYSTEM${color3}${hr 3}
${color2}${font}${color2}SWAP:${alignc}${swap}/${swapmax}${alignr}${swapperc}%
${color3}${swapbar}
${color2}Root:${alignc}${fs_free /}/${fs_size /}${alignr}${fs_free_perc /}%
${color3}${fs_bar /}
${color2}Home:${alignc}${fs_free /home}/${fs_size /home}${alignr}${fs_free_perc /home}%
${color3}${fs_bar /home}
${color2}Other:${alignc}${fs_free /backup_stuff_here}/${fs_size /backup_stuff_here}${alignr}${fs_free_perc /backup_stuff_here}%
${color3}${fs_bar /backup_stuff_here}
${color5}${font Sans:style=Bold:size=10}PROCESSES${color3}${hr 3}${font}${color2}
Processes:${alignr}${processes} (${running_processes} running)
Load:${alignr}${loadavg}
NAME${alignr} PID    CPU  MEM
${top name 1} ${alignr}${top pid 1} ${top cpu 1} ${top mem 1}
${top name 2} ${alignr}${top pid 2} ${top cpu 2} ${top mem 2}
${top name 3} ${alignr}${top pid 3} ${top cpu 3} ${top mem 3}
${top name 4} ${alignr}${top pid 4} ${top cpu 4} ${top mem 4}
${top name 5} ${alignr}${top pid 5} ${top cpu 5} ${top mem 5}
${color5}${font Sans:style=Bold:size=10}NETWORK${color3}${hr 3}
${color2}${font}IP Address:${alignr}${addr eth0}
Total Download:${alignr}${totaldown eth0}
Total Upload:${alignr}${totalup eth0}
Up Speed:${alignr}${upspeed eth0} Kb/s
Down Speed:${alignr}${downspeed eth0} Kb/s
${color5}${font Sans:style=Bold:size=10}TO DO LIST${color3}${hr 3}
${color2}${font}${execi 30 cat $HOME/.TODO.txt}
${font Mono:size=8}${execi 30 cat $HOME/.moo.txt}
```

The panel is located at the bottom of the screen, changed the opacity via the compiz options. If anyone wants to know how I did that, [click here]("http://zyxyellowxyz.deviantart.com/art/06-12-2009-125700839")

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2009-06-13
> **Dirk.R.Gently said:**
> Why do people bother with 75hz?  60hz is about what the human eye can process.

Err, the human eye can process more than that. The entire point of increasing the refresh rate is to reduce flicker and eye-strain. Doesn't always work in practice; my old CRT was unbearable to look at in 75hz mode.

---

### Post by darthmob on 2009-06-13

> Why do people bother with 75hz?  60hz is about what the human eye can process.

Film frame rate is normal 25 frames per sec.

### Post by pelle.k on 2009-06-13
> Why do people bother with 75hz? 60hz is about what the human eye can process.
Maybe you're not very sensitive to those things, but many people get terrible headaches < 80 hz (on crt, that is). It's not so much an issue on LCD monitors though.

### Post by Islington on 2009-06-13

### Post by londonali1010 on 2009-06-13
> **Sarai the Geek said:**
> Hideous, or just blinding...?

You decide.

Oooh! My Little Pony! Love it :KS

I've been working on Conky all day...Fun! I have converted from AWN to gnome-do, but actually I like the normal mode more than Docky. I only used Docky because I needed somewhere to keep my window list...In the end, I have hidden both panels, for the symmetry, and because I like having my systray open somewhere and so I can see the clock if I've got a maximised window open. I've also kept the menu on the upper panel, but I don't really use it now that I've gotten used to gnome-do. And my window list is on the bottom panel (what can I say, I grew up on Windows). Now my idle memory is better, because gnome-do takes less juice in normal mode...

I also took the daring (okay, for me!) move of getting rid of window titles...I figured, hey, I know what's in the window because it's open! I don't use shade, so it was a little redundant, and has freed up some screen real estate :D Anyway, enough of my wittering on...
[ATTACH]117544[/ATTACH][ATTACH]117545[/ATTACH]

### Post by asdfhjkla on 2009-06-15
> **ad_267 said:**
> That is really nice, good work. :guitar:

Only thing I would change is make the panel a little thinner and have a bit more contrast between the text and background in your GTK colour scheme.

Just found your [tintwizard]("http://www.uluga.ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?p=7451069") project too by the way, that looks quite interesting.

Thanks. I agree - panel kinda contrasts with the rest of it. I should make it thinner :)

> **easybake said:**
> what is the music player?

It's called [ncmpcpp]("http://unkart.ovh.org/ncmpcpp/"), and it is a client for [mpd]("http://mpd.wikia.com/wiki/Music_Player_Daemon_Wiki"). It felt a bit strange at first to control my music through a terminal but now it's just so much more convenient! :p

> **eightmillion said:**
> Looks like cplay. Also, asdfhjkla, could you link your wallpaper?

Sure - you can get it [here]("http://farm4.static.flickr.com/3128/2502280611_a2db100e60_o.jpg").

> **Wra!th said:**
> Mind posting your GTK theme's name (or the actual theme...)?

It's called "Candido-Light" and requires the Candido engine which you can find [here]("http://candido.berlios.de/pages/engine.php"). I can't remember if this theme was installed along with the engine so I've attached it :)

### Post by PurposeOfReason on 2009-06-15
> **el mariachi said:**
> I wish my terminals were as colorful....:(:(
It doesn't take all that much work. Just get a good vim colorscheme, LS_COLORS for your bash needs, man page colors, and an ncmpcpp config and you're set.

### Post by narf41 on 2009-06-15
for flat bakcground use glass engine, the same value for first and second color with some transparency, and set all other colors to 100% transparency
the icons are centered by default

### Post by ad_267 on 2009-06-16
It's in the default Ubuntu repositories. ```
sudo apt-get install kde4-style-bespin
```

I'm not sure how up to date that is, you're probably better off with the version from the subversion repository.

Edit: You need to make sure the file is executable, "chmod a+x configure"

### Post by eightmillion on 2009-06-16
> **kenleyrob said:**
> Very nice, which icon theme is that?
Thanks. It's iKon. I think lzfy has a link in his sig. Edit: [link]("http://dl.getdropbox.com/u/803597/iKon_2.tar.gz")
> **Sand & Mercury said:**
> Where is everyone getting the Air plasma theme from?? :| I've tried the neon nightly builds and Kubuntu's experimental 4.3 ppa, and the Karmic alpha and I can't find the theme present in any of them. Am I missing something or just retarded?
I don't know whether it comes with a Kubuntu PPA install, but you can get it right from the SVN repository. Just navigate to ~/.kde/share/apps/desktoptheme/ and check it out with:
```
svn co svn://anonsvn.kde.org/home/kde/trunk/playground/base/plasma/desktoptheme/air/
``` 
Then you should be able to select it from the desktop settings dialog.

---

### Post by G@B0 on 2009-06-16
> **Sand & Mercury said:**
> Where is everyone getting the Air plasma theme from?? :| I've tried the neon nightly builds and Kubuntu's experimental 4.3 ppa, and the Karmic alpha and I can't find the theme present in any of them. Am I missing something or just retarded?

From svn.
Put this is the terminal:
```
svn checkout svn://anonsvn.kde.org/home/kde/trunk/playground/base/plasma/desktoptheme/air

```

Then put it ~/.kde/share/apps/desktoptheme

> **Sarai the Geek said:**
> Arcade Fire FTW! Funeral is one of my very favorite albums- so in addition to master KDE theming skillz, you also have mighty fine taste in music. Hats off to you!

I saw Arcade Fire live several years ago, right after Funeral came out,  in Columbia, Missouri. The place that they played was so small that the drummer was able to use the rafters as a makeshift percussion instrument from time to time, standing up and beating his sticks against them. The "stage" in the place was clearly an afterthought. We even got to stick around and chat with the members of the band afterwards. I've seen hundreds of bands live, and that was definitely one of the more memorable.

---

### Post by Mark76 on 2009-06-17
Amidst all this KDE love, here's mine for today

### Post by Sand &amp; Mercury on 2009-06-17
> **G@B0 said:**
> From svn.
Put this is the terminal:
```
svn checkout svn://anonsvn.kde.org/home/kde/trunk/playground/base/plasma/desktoptheme/air

```

Then put it ~/.kde/share/apps/desktoptheme

> **eightmillion said:**
> Thanks. It's iKon. I think lzfy has a link in his sig. Edit: [link]("http://dl.getdropbox.com/u/803597/iKon_2.tar.gz")

I don't know whether it comes with a Kubuntu PPA install, but you can get it right from the SVN repository. Just navigate to ~/.kde/share/apps/desktoptheme/ and check it out with:
```
svn co svn://anonsvn.kde.org/home/kde/trunk/playground/base/plasma/desktoptheme/air/
``` 
Then you should be able to select it from the desktop settings dialog.
Thanks guys!

---

### Post by jordanmthomas on 2009-06-17
> **Islington said:**
> you best be jokin, it is pretty and clean, only thing I would change is the font.


mind sharing that conky setup? ...it is conky right?

.conky-mpd
```

#avoid flicker
double_buffer yes

#own window to run simultanious 2 or more conkys
own_window yes
own_window_transparent yes
own_window_type override
own_window_hints undecorate,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager 

#borders
draw_borders no
border_margin 1

#shades
draw_shades no

#position
gap_x 10
gap_y 20
alignment middle_left

#behaviour
update_interval 5

#colour
default_color ffffff
#default_shade_color cccccc
own_window_colour 222222

#font
use_xft yes
xftfont Myriad Pro:pixelsize=10

#to prevent window from moving
use_spacer none
minimum_size 100 0
maximum_width 600

TEXT
${color white}${font Myriad Pro:style=Bold:pixelsize=16}${mpd_smart}
${color white}on ${font Myriad Pro:style=Bold:pixelsize=16}${mpd_album} at ${mpd_bitrate} kbps$color
${color white}${font Myriad Pro:style=Bold:pixelsize=16}[${mpd_elapsed}/${mpd_length}] 
Volume:  ${font Myriad Pro:pixelsize=16}${mpd_vol}

${color white}${font Myriad Pro:style=Bold:pixelsize=16}ESSID:  ${font Myriad Pro:pixelsize}${wireless_essid eth0}
${color white}${font Myriad Pro:style=Bold:pixelsize=16}LINK:  ${font Myriad Pro:pixelsize}${wireless_link_bar 5, 100 eth0}
${color white}${font Myriad Pro:style=Bold:pixelsize=16}TX:  ${font Myriad Pro:pixelsize}${upspeedf eth0}KiB/s        ${color white}${font Myriad Pro:style=Bold:pixelsize=16}RX:  ${font Myriad Pro:pixelsize}${downspeedf eth0}KiB/s
${color white}${upspeedgraph eth0 20,70}            ${downspeedgraph eth0 20,70}

${color white}${font Myriad Pro:style=Bold:pixelsize=16}ACTIVE PROCESSES:  ${font Myriad Pro:pixelsize}${running_processes}

```

.conky-clock
```

#avoid flicker
double_buffer yes

#own window to run simultanious 2 or more conkys
own_window yes
own_window_transparent yes
own_window_type override
own_window_hints undecorate,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager 

#borders
draw_borders no
border_margin 1

#shades
draw_shades no

#position
gap_x 300
gap_y 280
alignment center

#behaviour
update_interval 1

#colour
default_color ffffff
#default_shade_color cccccc
own_window_colour 222222

#font
use_xft yes
xftfont Calibri:pixelsize=10

#to prevent window from moving
use_spacer no
minimum_size 100 0


TEXT
${color white}${font Myriad Pro:style=Bold:pixelsize=80}${alignc}${time %I:%M %P}$color
${color white}${font Myriad Pro:pixelsize=70}${alignc}${time %A %B %d %Y}$color

```

.conky-system
```

#avoid flicker
double_buffer yes

#own window to run simultanious 2 or more conkys
own_window yes
own_window_transparent yes
own_window_type override
own_window_hints undecorate,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager 

#borders
draw_borders no
border_margin 1

#shades
draw_shades no

#position
gap_x 10
gap_y 15
alignment middle_right

#behaviour
update_interval 5

#colour
default_color ffffff
#default_shade_color cccccc
own_window_colour 222222

#font
use_xft yes
xftfont Myriad Pro:pixelsize=10

#to prevent window from moving
use_spacer no
minimum_size 100 0


TEXT
${color white}${font Myriad Pro:style=Bold:pixelsize=16}${nodename}$color
${color white}${font Myriad Pro:style=Bold:pixelsize=16}UP:  ${font Myriad Pro:pixelsize=16}${uptime}$color

${color white}${font Myriad Pro:style=Bold:pixelsize=16}MEM:  ${font Myriad Pro:pixelsize}${MEM}
${color white}${membar}$color

${color white}${font Myriad Pro:style=Bold:pixelsize=16}CPU:  ${font Myriad Pro:pixelsize}${CPU}%$color
${color white}${cpugraph}$color
${color white}${font Myriad Pro:style=Bold:pixelsize=16}LOAD:  ${font Myriad Pro:pixelsize}${loadavg}%$color
${color white}${loadgraph}$color

```

Sorry these are messy too, but they should be manageable at least.

### Post by Giant Speck on 2009-06-17
This theme is finally starting to come together.

I found an awesome panel background on deviantART and made a custom menu button just for it. The panel applets on the sides are locked so that things don't get pushed off into the transparent parts.

I didn't do much to the theme itself.  I did however, import some settings from a theme I scrapped a long time ago.

I recolored a wallpaper from Alexander_GG's "Colored Backgrounds pack" to match the overall color scheme.

Anyway, here are the details of these specific screenshots:

GTK:  Espresso 0.1pre (not yet released; don't ask for it)
Font:  Calibri 9
Panel:  [KDE Style]("http://xcracx.deviantart.com/art/Gnome-Panel-set1-KDE-style-120991146") (the panel is designed for a 1024-pixel-wide screen, so you will need to do what I did and edit it in GIMP)
Wallpaper:  [Colored Backgrounds]("http://alexander-gg.deviantart.com/art/Colored-Backgrounds-102172919")

If you have a question about my themes, please ask me here and not in a PM.

### Post by cc8balla on 2009-06-17
God Speck, you know how to turn brown into something amazing looking, good work!

The only thing that I want to know, is how in the world did you get the dropdown arrows on the bookmark toolbar to disappear? I've tried nearly everything I can think of.

Edit, nvm, I FINALLY got it. Heh. I was using this:

```
#PersonalToolbar .toolbarbutton-menu-dropmarker {display: none !important;}
```

When I simply should have used this:

```
.toolbarbutton-menu-dropmarker {display: none !important;}
```

Dunno what I was thinking for the past half hour using the first one...I dont think I WAS thinking. Also, updated screens of my desktop. Want to make GNOME look as good as kde, heh

### Post by izizzle on 2009-06-17
Gnome-Do was designed for Gnome, true, but all it takes is a few libs and you're good to go with KDE or even XFCE. It works flawlessly (well, [almost]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=1188245")) and I find it to be a very worthwhile (and better-looking IMHO) replacement for the default panel.

### Post by Islington on 2009-06-17
> **eightmillion said:**
> I'm curious what gnome do does (besides docky) that krunner doesn't. It seems to me that they do the same thing, but I could be completely wrong.

what cant gnome do do? 

tweet? yes
open urls? yes
check google/wiki/yahoo/others? yes
tile your windows? yes
start an email message/im to someone? yes
calendar? yes
clock? yes
contacts? yes
dock? yes
launcher? yes
upload an image to imageshack? yes
terminal commands? yes
moving renaming playing with files and folders? yes
dictionary? yes
mount/unmount? yes

The plugin architecture is what really makes it powerful.I havent been playing around with krunner so much yet (just moved to kubuntu for serious) but krunner really doesnt have a scratch on Do's plugins.

### Post by gymophett on 2009-06-19
> **londonali1010 said:**
> Hey, that's nice! Shiki Human?

Also, what theme did you use for Firefox?  It looks nice.

Wrong wrong my friend, and nice it is. :)
Download Wasp theme pack.
I use Wasp-Alt as controls and Window Border.
Balanzan Icons.
Extremely nice, clean and professional looking.
Wallpaper from zixpk.
I don't have a Firefox theme installed. :)
To change your Firefox to look minimal with your theme, follow these steps.
Add the Tinymenu Firefox add-on.
Right click somewhere around the top of Firefox, around the address bar.
When you see a list, Navigation Toolbar, Bookmarks toolbar, and Customization, click Customization.
Drag your back and forward buttons, refresh, stop, home, address bar, and search bar to the top. Restart Firefox. Uncheck Navigation and Bookmarks toolbars. And that's all. :)
This will be great for your netbook!
Also, to get more space, go to view and uncheck status bar.
Happy browsing. :)

---

### Post by asdfhjkla on 2009-06-20
> **Giant Speck said:**
> I looked at the man page for trayer, and it didn't show a "grow" option.

Though, I installed it, and gave it a fixed width and height and set the alignment to right, and it did basically what I wanted.  My problem, though, is that when I place it on top of my panel and then click the panel, it disappears.

Apologies - it's stalonetray that has the grow option (where's the facepalm smiley? :p)

I just tried it in gnome and noticed the same problem. Even setting trayer as dock doesn't work because gnome-panel has window type "dock". Do you have the CompizConfig Settings Manager? If you enable the Window Rules plugin under the Window Management section, you can add ```
class=Gnome-panel
``` to the "Below" matches. I don't normally use compiz so I'm not sure if this will have any side effects for other stuff you use.

---

### Post by Giant Speck on 2009-06-20
> **asdfhjkla said:**
> Apologies - it's stalonetray that has the grow option (where's the facepalm smiley? :p)

I just tried it in gnome and noticed the same problem. Even setting trayer as dock doesn't work because gnome-panel has window type "dock". Do you have the CompizConfig Settings Manager? If you enable the Window Rules plugin under the Window Management section, you can add ```
class=Gnome-panel
``` to the "Below" matches. I don't normally use compiz so I'm not sure if this will have any side effects for other stuff you use.

This worked, except instead of adding gnome-panel to "below," I added trayer to "above."  :)

Thanks for the help!

### Post by asdfhjkla on 2009-06-21
> **xX-Felipao-Xx said:**
> I need help here !
Check out my screenshot and look at the toolbar in gedit, all the toolbars are like that one and I'd like to change their colour to #f5f5f5, but the fact is that I don't know where, I've searched in .gtkrc but that blackish colour doesn't appears in the code... 

What can I do? how can i change it??

thanks :)

Do you mean the black menubar?

Try setting the ```
bg[NORMAL]
``` property in the style ```
style "theme-menubar"
``` If your theme doesn't have this style, scroll down to the bottom of the gtkrc and see what style has been applied to ```
class "*MenuBar*"
```

Hopefully that *should* be what needs changed :)

---

### Post by Mazza558 on 2009-06-21
I'm going to adapt the elementary metacity theme for use in Futurelooks 3.3 (which will also include the elementary icons (I've asked permission to use/adapt them). Yes, it looks like OSX at the moment, this is because I haven't added the original buttons in yet. But, as you can see, the base is there and looks a lot nicer than the previous incarnation. 
Now all I need to do is figure out how on earth to adapt elementary's metacity to use the futurelooks icons. I'm also having to fight the ridiculous ".theme" file which refuses to acknowledge the existence of the metacity theme at all. 

I have to say, I'm pretty pleased with how this'll all turn out (hopefully) - DanRabbit (who made the metacity theme for elementary) has shown that you can make decent stuff with metacity after all. 

"I can't believe it's not emerald!" :P


So by the time FL3.3 is out, the end-user will have the metacity theme and emerald theme to choose from, each offering a different look - the metacity being more "slab-like" and emerald more transparent.

### Post by Daisuke_Aramaki on 2009-06-21
> **el mariachi said:**
> seriously: beautiful terminals-how? :D

Simple. Define some colors, font specifications, et., in your .Xdefaults (assuming you know about Xdefaults and what it can do as such). As far as vim goes, get a good vim color scheme and use it. You can even define the scheme to be used by default when you want to edit files with vim, by defining the same in your .vimrc.

Also you can define prompt behavior whether the shell you are using is bash or zsh. 

If you need my configs, let me know.

---

### Post by Daisuke_Aramaki on 2009-06-22
> **mjheagle8 said:**
> what terminal and panel do you use? and how do you get the command in the title of the terminal?

You could see clearly in the screenshot, the terminal is xterm. And there is no third party panel used, just the default fluxbox toolbar, themed to go with  the fluxbox theme.

The fancy command title is set in my .zshrc. If you want it to be displayed, just copy and paste the text below in your .zshrc.

```

## display fancy terminal title
case $TERM in
	*xterm*|(u)rxvt|(u|dt|k|E)term)
	## display user@host and full dir in *term title
	precmd () {
		print -Pn  "\033]0;%n@%m: %~ (%l)\007"
		#print -Pn "\033]0;%n@%m%#  %~ %l  %w :: %T\a" ## or use this
		}
	## display user@host and name of current process in *term title
	preexec () {
		print -Pn "\033]0;%n@%m <$1> %~ (%l)\007"
		#print -Pn "\033]0;%n@%m%#  <$1>  %~ %l  %w :: %T\a" ## or use this
		}
	;;
esac

```

Hope that helps

### Post by pelle.k on 2009-06-22
Hey **perfectska04**, just a quick rant here, because i saw the discussion on gnomelooks regarding the arctic/aluminium icons, and since i don't have a gnome-looks account i post here instead...
"Arctic" did look stunning, but if i were to choose between the dark and light "Aluminium", the light did look much better. My vote goes to "Arctic" though.
Maybe you could start using "mixed" colors if arctic doesn't look to good with devices. Say, use a standard gray/white with all "devices", but colorize the rest of the system?

Something i do quite often, is to use "neutral theme" as a base, and the colorize the most common, and visual elements, in a particular color, such as common "toolbar items" (go-* etc) and places (folder*, user-*). I would imagine that's not a solution for you, being the "perfectionist" you are... ;)

Also i was a little sad to see the lightbrown dust go, but the dark brown is also really pretty, so that is no big loss. However, a light brown icon theme would still be welcome in the future. I must say the folder icons (old gnome-dust) did look a little too gray actually, so maybe using a little more light brown than the "shortlived" gnome-dust would do it.

BTW thanks for all the hard work!

I would imagine that's not a solution for you, being the "perfectionist" you are... ;)

Also i was a little sad to see the lightbrown dust go, but the dark brown is also really pretty, so that is no big loss. However, a light brown icon theme would still be welcome in the future. BTW thanks for all the hard work!

Arctic or Aluminium didn't really work out. They pretty much looked as if I just ran a grayscale script on all the icons, which isn't necessarily bad, but it looked rather dull and boring in usage. Then again, in the future, I might perfect the Aluminium palette so that it looks well with Shiki and make it inheritable by all the other sets, so the package ends up smaller than 10MB and other artists can just inherit the gnome-colors base and make any color scheme they want easily. As for the short-lived light dust, it was just a bad decision as the folders looked almost like packages and the color palette reminded people of bodily functions rather than chocolate. It's still uploaded to mediafire for archiving as gnome-caramel, but it was completely dropped.

### Post by narf41 on 2009-06-23
created a new sreenlet theme for sensors and netmonitor, fitting to the awn icons
[[img]http://ubuntu-pics.de/thumb/17005/orihawn_45Z25k.png[/img]](http://ubuntu-pics.de/bild/17005/orihawn_45Z25k.png)

you can place awn left or right from center: gconf editor>>apps>>awn>>bar>>bar_pos
value from 0 to 1 in 0.1 steps (0=left, 0.5=center, 1=right)

### Post by cc8balla on 2009-06-24
> **BDNiner said:**
> Details please. Especially what borders are you using and how did you get the panel to look so great. is it AWN on the left? What is on the right? and how did you get AWN on the left?
Here is where I got nearly all the inspiration. [http://narf41.deviantart.com/](http://narf41.deviantart.com/)

This is the theme I'm using. [http://narf41.deviantart.com/art/gORIH-126795383](http://narf41.deviantart.com/art/gORIH-126795383) 

Icons are Meliae-Dark (although I may change to Meliae White)

That is awn on the left, trayer on the right. Clock is a screenlet, and the awn icons are [http://stopdreaming.deviantart.com/art/Albook-extended-782-png-95130593](http://stopdreaming.deviantart.com/art/Albook-extended-782-png-95130593)

I also hate any applet for awn that shows the gnome menu, so i cheated by making a top panel, shrinking it to autohide to 1, then setting the time that it will appear at something like 1000000000 ms. This way I can still click on the menu, and not have to have the whole panel appear. Kinda hides it too, which is niccccee. 

I've quoted narf41's orig post about how to move awn. 

> **narf41 said:**
> created a new sreenlet theme for sensors and netmonitor, fitting to the awn icons
[[img]http://ubuntu-pics.de/thumb/17005/orihawn_45Z25k.png[/img]](http://ubuntu-pics.de/bild/17005/orihawn_45Z25k.png)

you can place awn left or right from center: gconf editor>>apps>>awn>>bar>>bar_pos
value from 0 to 1 in 0.1 steps (0=left, 0.5=center, 1=right)

### Post by Fatal Toenail Infection on 2009-06-26
SpriteSODA:  [https://wiki.ubuntu.com/global_menu](https://wiki.ubuntu.com/global_menu)

This is my new desktop that I am rather proud of.  For the past several weeks I've debated switching to KDE after being a gnome user for two years now.  Visually, it is so far ahead of gnome, but I prefer the usability of gnome.  I tried using it last week, but there are some things that are just too different that I won't be able to get used to (not to mention the network manager is buggy and difficult to figure out).  So I decided to try installing plasma in gnome, and to my surprise it worked almost perfectly.  Here is my desktop with Aurora GTK and Glassified Plasma:

[[IMG]http://img191.imageshack.us/img191/9716/screenshotu.th.png[/IMG]](http://img191.imageshack.us/i/screenshotu.png/)

[[IMG]http://img524.imageshack.us/img524/4301/screenshot2ocg.th.png[/IMG]](http://img524.imageshack.us/i/screenshot2ocg.png/)

---

### Post by Fatal Toenail Infection on 2009-06-27
To be honest, there's not much to it.  I'm still very much a linux newbie, so I can try to explain my very best what I've done.  I believe I installed the kdebase-plasma package in synaptic (and the dependencies followed).  I may have also installed kdebase-workspace and kdebase-workspace-data.  Then, simply ALT-F2 and run plasma (first startup might take awhile) and eventually it will "grab" your desktop and take control of the wallpaper and add a panel at the botton.  You can add an entry to Startup Applications for plasma to have it start each time you log in.  I would suggest disabling the folder view that comes enabled by default because it will crash the entire plasma interface if you right click or perform other actions within it.  You can also run gconf-editor and browse to apps/nautilus/preferences and uncheck "show desktop" to disable the nautilus desktop running behind plasma.  I'm not sure if there's anything else...The top gnome panel can be configured any way you want really, but if you use a panel packground with transparency, it will show through to the "nautilus" desktop, so you will have to make sure that the wallpaper set in plasma is the same as the wallpaper set in gnome under "Appearance".

---
